Throughout the 20th century, most Anglophone scholars dismissed Verne as a genre writer for children and a na&#239;ve proponent of science and technology (despite strong evidence to the contrary on both counts), thus finding him more interesting as a technological "prophet" or as a subject of comparison to English-language writers such as <a href="/wiki/Edgar_Allan_Poe" title="Edgar Allan Poe">Edgar Allan Poe</a> and <a href="/wiki/H._G._Wells" title="H. G. Wells">H. G. Wells</a> than as a topic of literary study in his own right. This narrow view of Verne has undoubtedly been influenced by the poor-quality <a href="/wiki/Jules_Verne#English_translations" title="Jules Verne">English translations</a> and very loosely adapted <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_the_United_States" title="Cinema of the United States">Hollywood film</a> versions through which most American and British readers have discovered Verne.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans200033_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans200033-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEButcher1983_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEButcher1983-101">[100]</a></sup> However, since the mid-1980s a considerable number of serious English-language studies and translations have appeared, suggesting that a rehabilitation of Verne\'s Anglophone reputation may currently be underway.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Miller2009_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-Miller2009-102">[101]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans200034_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans200034-103">[102]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="English_translations">English translations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jules_Verne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: English translations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Translation of Verne into English began in 1852, when Verne\'s short story "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/A_Voyage_in_a_Balloon" title="A Voyage in a Balloon">A Voyage in a Balloon</a>" (1851) was published in the American journal <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sartain%27s_Magazine" title="Sartain\'s Magazine">Sartain\'s Union Magazine of Literature and Art</a></i> in a translation by Anne T. Wilbur.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans2005b117_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans2005b117-104">[103]</a></sup> Translation of his novels began in 1869 with William Lackland\'s translation of <i><a href="/wiki/Five_Weeks_in_a_Balloon" title="Five Weeks in a Balloon">Five Weeks in a Balloon</a></i> (originally published in 1863),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans2005b105_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans2005b105-105">[104]</a></sup> and continued steadily throughout Verne\'s lifetime, with publishers and hired translators often working in great haste to rush his most lucrative titles into English-language print.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans2005a80_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans2005a80-106">[105]</a></sup> Unlike Hetzel, who targeted all ages with his publishing strategies for the <i>Voyages extraordinaires</i>, the British and American publishers of Verne chose to market his books almost exclusively to young audiences; this business move, with its implication that Verne could be treated purely as a children\'s author, had a long-lasting effect on Verne\'s reputation in English-speaking countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Miller2009_102-1"><a href="#cite_note-Miller2009-102">[101]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans2005a117_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans2005a117-107">[106]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:A_Journey_to_the_Centre_of_the_Earth-1874.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="574" data-file-width="410" decoding="async" height="210" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/A_Journey_to_the_Centre_of_the_Earth-1874.jpg/150px-A_Journey_to_the_Centre_of_the_Earth-1874.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/A_Journey_to_the_Centre_of_the_Earth-1874.jpg/225px-A_Journey_to_the_Centre_of_the_Earth-1874.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/A_Journey_to_the_Centre_of_the_Earth-1874.jpg/300px-A_Journey_to_the_Centre_of_the_Earth-1874.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:A_Journey_to_the_Centre_of_the_Earth-1874.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An early edition of the notorious Griffith &amp; Farran adaptation of <i><a href="/wiki/Journey_to_the_Center_of_the_Earth" title="Journey to the Center of the Earth">Journey to the Center of the Earth</a></i></div></div></div>\n<p>These early English-language translations have been widely criticized for their extensive textual omissions, errors, and alterations, and are not considered adequate representations of Verne\'s actual novels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans2005a80_106-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans2005a80-106">[105]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Roberts_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-Roberts-108">[107]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Crichton_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-Crichton-109">[108]</a></sup> The British writer <a href="/wiki/Adam_Roberts_(British_writer)" title="Adam Roberts (British writer)">Adam Roberts</a>, in an essay for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> titled "Jules Verne deserves a better translation service", commented: "I\'d always liked reading Jules Verne and I\'ve read most of his novels; but it wasn\'t until recently that I really understood I hadn\'t been reading Jules Verne at all.... It\'s a bizarre situation for a world-famous writer to be in. Indeed, I can\'t think of a major writer who has been so poorly served by translation."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Roberts_108-1"><a href="#cite_note-Roberts-108">[107]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Similarly, the American novelist <a href="/wiki/Michael_Crichton" title="Michael Crichton">Michael Crichton</a> observed:\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303468">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Verne\'s prose is lean and fast-moving in a peculiarly modern way &#8230; [but] Verne has been particularly ill-served by his English translators. At best they have provided us with clunky, choppy, tone-deaf prose. At worst&#8212;as in the notorious 1872 "translation" [of <i><a href="/wiki/Journey_to_the_Center_of_the_Earth" title="Journey to the Center of the Earth">Journey to the Center of the Earth</a></i>] published by Griffith &amp; Farran&#8212;they have blithely altered the text, giving Verne\'s characters new names, and adding whole pages of their own invention, thus effectively obliterating the meaning and tone of Verne\'s original.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Crichton_109-1"><a href="#cite_note-Crichton-109">[108]</a></sup>\n</p></blockquote>\n<p>Since 1965, a considerable number of more accurate English translations of Verne have appeared. However, the highly criticized older translations continue to be republished, due to their <a href="/wiki/Public_domain" title="Public domain">public domain</a> status and in many cases their easy availability in online sources.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Miller2009_102-2"><a href="#cite_note-Miller2009-102">[101]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Relationship_with_science_fiction">Relationship with science fiction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jules_Verne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Relationship with science fiction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The relationship between Verne\'s <i>Voyages extraordinaires</i> and the literary genre science fiction is a complex one. Verne, like <a href="/wiki/H._G._Wells" title="H. G. Wells">H. G. Wells</a>, is frequently cited as one of the founders of the genre, and his profound influence on its development is indisputable; however, many earlier writers, such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lucian_of_Samosata" title="Lucian of Samosata">Lucian of Samosata</a>, <a href="/wiki/Voltaire" title="Voltaire">Voltaire</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mary_Shelley" title="Mary Shelley">Mary Shelley</a>, have also been cited as creators of science fiction, an unavoidable ambiguity arising from the vague definition and <a href="/wiki/History_of_science_fiction" title="History of science fiction">history of the genre</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Roberts48_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-Roberts48-6">[6]</a></sup>\n</p><p>A primary issue at the heart of the dispute is the question of whether Verne\'s works count as science fiction to begin with. <a href="/wiki/Maurice_Renard" title="Maurice Renard">Maurice Renard</a> claimed that Verne "never wrote a single sentence of scientific-marvelous".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[109]</a></sup> Verne himself argued repeatedly in interviews that his novels were not meant to be read as scientific, saying "I have invented nothing."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESherard1903&#167;5_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESherard1903&#167;5-111">[110]</a></sup> His own goal was rather to "depict the earth [and] at the same time to realize a very high ideal of beauty of style",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESherard1894&#167;4_71-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESherard1894&#167;4-71">[70]</a></sup> as he pointed out in an example:\n</p>\n<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>I wrote <i><a href="/wiki/Five_Weeks_in_a_Balloon" title="Five Weeks in a Balloon">Five Weeks in a Balloon</a>,</i> not as a story about ballooning, but as a story about Africa. I always was greatly interested in geography and travel, and I wanted to give a romantic description of Africa. Now, there was no means of taking my travellers through Africa otherwise than in a balloon, and that is why a balloon is introduced.&#8230; I may say that at the time I wrote the novel, as now, I had no faith in the possibility of ever steering balloons&#8230;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESherard1894&#167;4_71-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESherard1894&#167;4-71">[70]</a></sup>\n</p></blockquote>\n<p>Closely related to Verne\'s science-fiction reputation is the often-repeated claim that he is a "<a href="/wiki/Prophet" title="Prophet">prophet</a>" of scientific progress, and that many of his novels involve elements of technology that were fantastic for his day but later became commonplace.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans19881_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans19881-112">[111]</a></sup> These claims have a long history, especially in America, but the modern scholarly consensus is that such claims of prophecy are heavily exaggerated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans19882_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans19882-113">[112]</a></sup> In a 1961 article critical of <i>Twenty Thousand Leagues Under the Sea</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">\'</span>s scientific accuracy, <a href="/wiki/Theodore_L._Thomas" title="Theodore L. Thomas">Theodore L. Thomas</a> speculated that Verne\'s storytelling skill and readers misremembering a book they read as children caused people to "remember things from it that are not there. The impression that the novel contains valid scientific prediction seems to grow as the years roll by".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thomas196112_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-thomas196112-114">[113]</a></sup> As with science fiction, Verne himself flatly denied that he was a futuristic prophet, saying that any connection between scientific developments and his work was "mere coincidence" and attributing his indisputable scientific accuracy to his extensive research: "even before I began writing stories, I always took numerous notes out of every book, newspaper, magazine, or scientific report that I came across."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBelloc1895_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBelloc1895-115">[114]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jules_Verne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Legacy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cesantes_Redondela_Galicia.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="670" data-file-width="937" decoding="async" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Cesantes_Redondela_Galicia.jpg/220px-Cesantes_Redondela_Galicia.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Cesantes_Redondela_Galicia.jpg/330px-Cesantes_Redondela_Galicia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Cesantes_Redondela_Galicia.jpg/440px-Cesantes_Redondela_Galicia.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cesantes_Redondela_Galicia.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Monument to Jules Verne in <a href="/wiki/Redondela" title="Redondela">Redondela</a>, Spain</div></div></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cultural_influence_of_Jules_Verne" title="Cultural influence of Jules Verne">Cultural influence of Jules Verne</a></div>\n<p>Verne\'s novels have had a wide influence on both literary and scientific works; writers known to have been influenced by Verne include <a href="/wiki/Marcel_Aym%C3%A9" title="Marcel Aym&#233;">Marcel Aym&#233;</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roland_Barthes" title="Roland Barthes">Roland Barthes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ren%C3%A9_Barjavel" title="Ren&#233; Barjavel">Ren&#233; Barjavel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michel_Butor" title="Michel Butor">Michel Butor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blaise_Cendrars" title="Blaise Cendrars">Blaise Cendrars</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Claudel" title="Paul Claudel">Paul Claudel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jean_Cocteau" title="Jean Cocteau">Jean Cocteau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Mauriac" title="Fran&#231;ois Mauriac">Fran&#231;ois Mauriac</a>, <a href="/wiki/Raymond_Roussel" title="Raymond Roussel">Raymond Roussel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Claude_Roy_(poet)" title="Claude Roy (poet)">Claude Roy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Julio_Cort%C3%A1zar" title="Julio Cort&#225;zar">Julio Cort&#225;zar</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Antoine_Saint-Exup%C3%A9ry" title="Antoine Saint-Exup&#233;ry">Antoine Saint-Exup&#233;ry</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jean-Paul_Sartre" title="Jean-Paul Sartre">Jean-Paul Sartre</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans200024_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans200024-116">[115]</a></sup> while scientists and explorers who acknowledged Verne\'s inspiration have included <a href="/wiki/Richard_E._Byrd" title="Richard E. Byrd">Richard E. Byrd</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yuri_Gagarin" title="Yuri Gagarin">Yuri Gagarin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Simon_Lake" title="Simon Lake">Simon Lake</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hubert_Lyautey" title="Hubert Lyautey">Hubert Lyautey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guglielmo_Marconi" title="Guglielmo Marconi">Guglielmo Marconi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fridtjof_Nansen" title="Fridtjof Nansen">Fridtjof Nansen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Konstantin_Tsiolkovsky" title="Konstantin Tsiolkovsky">Konstantin Tsiolkovsky</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wernher_von_Braun" title="Wernher von Braun">Wernher von Braun</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEButcher1983_101-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEButcher1983-101">[100]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Jack_Parsons_(rocket_engineer)" title="Jack Parsons (rocket engineer)">Jack Parsons</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPendle200533&#8211;40,_42&#8211;43_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPendle200533&#8211;40,_42&#8211;43-117">[116]</a></sup> He is credited with helping inspire the <i><a href="/wiki/Steampunk" title="Steampunk">steampunk</a></i> genre, a literary and social movement that glamorizes science fiction based on 19th-century technology.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETeague201328_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETeague201328-118">[117]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPercec2014220_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPercec2014220-119">[118]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Ray_Bradbury" title="Ray Bradbury">Ray Bradbury</a> summed up Verne\'s influence on literature and science the world over by saying: "We are all, in one way or another, the children of Jules Verne."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[119]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jules_Verne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Footnotes">Footnotes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jules_Verne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Footnotes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-fuye-9"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-fuye_9-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFJules-Verne1976">Jules-Verne 1976</a>, p.&#160;1: "On his mother\'s side, Verne is known to be descended from one \'N. Allott, Scotsman\', who came to France to serve in the Scots Guards of Louis XI and rose to earn a title (in 1462). He built his castle, complete with dovecote or <i>fuye</i> (a privilege in the royal gift), near Loudun in Anjou and took the noble name of Allotte de la Fuye."</span>\n</li>\n</ol></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jules_Verne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 20em; -webkit-column-width: 20em; column-width: 20em; list-style-type: decimal;">\n<ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-JCW-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-JCW_1-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><i><a href="/wiki/John_C._Wells#Longman_Pronunciation_Dictionary" title="John C.
